F<.perltidyrc> file in the home directory, and then for a system-wide
file F</usr/local/etc/perltidyrc>, and then it will look for
F</etc/perltidyrc>.  Note that these last two system-wide files do not
have a leading dot.  Further system-dependent information will be found
in the INSTALL file distributed with perltidy.

This file is free format, and simply a list of parameters, just as they
would be entered on a command line.  Any number of lines may be used,
with any number of parameters per line, although it may be easiest to
read with one parameter per line.  Blank lines are ignored, and text
after a '#' is ignored to the end of a line.

Here is an example of a F<.perltidyrc> file:

  # This is a simple of a .perltidyrc configuration file
  # This implements a highly spaced style
  -se    # errors to standard error output
  -w     # show all warnings
  -bl	 # braces on new lines
  -pt=0  # parens not tight at all
  -bt=0  # braces not tight
  -sbt=0 # square brackets not tight

The parameters in the F<.perltidyrc> file are installed first, so any
parameters given on the command line will have priority over them.  

To avoid confusion, perltidy ignores any command in the .perltidyrc
file which would cause some kind of dump and an exit.  These are:

 -h -v -ddf -dln -dop -dsn -dtt -dwls -dwrs -ss

There are several options may be helpful in debugging a F<.perltidyrc>
file:  

=over 4

=item *

A very helpful command is B<--dump-profile> or B<-dpro>.  It writes a
list of all configuration filenames tested to standard output, and 
if a file is found, it dumps the content to standard output before
exiting.  So, to find out where perltidy looks for its configuration
files, and which one if any it selects, just enter 

  perltidy -dpro

=item *

It may be simplest to develop and test configuration files with
alternative names, and invoke them with B<-pro=filename> on the command
line.  Then rename the desired file to F<.perltidyrc> when finished.

=item *

The parameters in the F<.perltidyrc> file can be switched off with 
the B<-npro> option.

=item *

The commands B<--dump-options>, B<--dump-defaults>, B<--dump-long-names>,
and B<--dump-short-names>, all described below, may all be helpful.

=back

=item Creating a new abbreviation

A special notation is available for use in a F<.perltidyrc> file
for creating an abbreviation for a group
of options.  This can be used to create a
shorthand for one or more styles which are frequently, but not always,
used.  The notation is to group the options within curly braces which
are preceded by the name of the alias (without leading dashes), like this:

	newword {
	-opt1
	-opt2
	}

where B<newword> is the abbreviation, and B<opt1>, etc, are existing parameters
I<or other abbreviations>.  The main syntax requirement is that
the new abbreviation must begin on a new line.
Space before and after the curly braces is optional.
For a
specific example, the following line

	airy {-bl -pt=0 -bt=0 -sbt=0}

could be placed in a F<.perltidyrc> file, and then invoked at will with

	perltidy -airy somefile.pl

(Either C<-airy> or C<--airy> may be used).

=item Skipping leading non-perl commands with B<-x> or B<--look-for-hash-bang>

If your script has leading lines of system commands or other text which
are not valid perl code, and which are separated from the start of the
perl code by a "hash-bang" line, ( a line of the form C<#!...perl> ),
you must use the B<-x> flag to tell perltidy not to parse and format any
lines before the "hash-bang" line.  This option also invokes perl with a
-x flag when checking the syntax.  This option was originally added to
allow perltidy to parse interactive VMS scripts, but it should be used
for any script which is normally invoked with C<perl -x>.

=item  Making a file unreadable

The goal of perltidy is to improve the readability of files, but there
are two commands which have the opposite effect, B<--mangle> and
B<--extrude>.  They are actually
merely aliases for combinations of other parameters.  Both of these
strip all possible whitespace, but leave comments and pod documents,
so that they are essentially reversible.  The
difference between these is that B<--mangle> puts the fewest possible
line breaks in a script while B<--extrude> puts the maximum possible.
Note that these options do not provided any meaningful obfuscation, because
perltidy can be used to reformat the files.  They were originally
developed to help test the tokenization logic of perltidy, but they
have other uses.
One use for B<--mangle> is the following:

  perltidy --mangle myfile.pl -st | perltidy -o myfile.pl.new

This will form the maximum possible number of one-line blocks (see next
section), and can sometimes help clean up a badly formatted script.

A similar technique can be used with B<--extrude> instead of B<--mangle>
to make the minimum number of one-line blocks.

Another use for B<--mangle> is to combine it with B<-dac> to reduce
the file size of a perl script.

=item  One-line blocks 

There are a few points to note regarding one-line blocks.  A one-line
block is something like this,

	if ($x > 0) { $y = 1 / $x }  

where the contents within the curly braces is short enough to fit
on a single line.

With few exceptions, perltidy retains existing one-line blocks, if it
is possible within the line-length constraint, but it does not attempt
to form new ones.  In other words, perltidy will try to follow the
one-line block style of the input file.

If an existing one-line block is longer than the maximum line length,
however, it will be broken into multiple lines.  When this happens, perltidy
checks for and adds any optional terminating semicolon (unless the B<-nasc>
option is used) if the block is a code block.  

The main exception is that perltidy will attempt to form new one-line
blocks following the keywords C<map>, C<eval>, and C<sort>, because
these code blocks are often small and most clearly displayed in a single
line.

One-line block rules can conflict with the cuddled-else option.  When
the cuddled-else option is used, perltidy retains existing one-line
blocks, even if they do not obey cuddled-else formatting.

Occasionally, when one-line blocks get broken because they exceed the
available line length, the formatting will violate the requested brace style.
If this happens, reformatting the script a second time should correct
the problem.

=item  Debugging 

The following flags are available for debugging:

B<--dump-defaults> or B<-ddf> will write the default option set to standard output and quit

B<--dump-profile> or B<-dpro>  will write the name of the current 
configuration file and its contents to standard output and quit.

B<--dump-options> or B<-dop>  will write current option set to standard
output and quit.  

B<--dump-long-names> or B<-dln>  will write all command line long names (passed 
to Get_options) to standard output and quit.

B<--dump-short-names>  or B<-dsn> will write all command line short names 
to standard output and quit.

B<--dump-token-types> or B<-dtt>  will write a list of all token types 
to standard output and quit.

B<--dump-want-left-space> or B<-dwls>  will write the hash %want_left_space
to standard output and quit.  See the section on controlling whitespace
around tokens.

B<--dump-want-right-space> or B<-dwrs>  will write the hash %want_right_space
to standard output and quit.  See the section on controlling whitespace
around tokens.

B<-DEBUG>  will write a file with extension F<.DEBUG> for each input file 
showing the tokenization of all lines of code.

=item Working with MakeMaker, AutoLoader and SelfLoader

The first $VERSION line of a file which might be eval'd by MakeMaker
is passed through unchanged except for indentation.  
Use B<--nopass-version-line>, or B<-npvl>, to deactivate this feature.

If the AutoLoader module is used, perltidy will continue formatting
code after seeing an __END__ line.
Use B<--nolook-for-autoloader>, or B<-nlal>, to deactivate this feature.

Likewise, if the SelfLoader module is used, perltidy will continue formatting
code after seeing a __DATA__ line.
Use B<--nolook-for-selfloader>, or B<-nlsl>, to deactivate this feature.

=item Working around problems with older version of Perl 

Perltidy contains a number of rules which help avoid known subtleties
and problems with older versions of perl, and these rules always
take priority over whatever formatting flags have been set.  For example,
perltidy will usually avoid starting a new line with a bareword, because
this might cause problems if C<use strict> is active.

There is no way to override these rules.

=back

=head1 HTML OPTIONS

=over 4

=item  The B<-html> master switch

The flag B<-html> causes perltidy to write an html file with extension
F<.html>.  So, for example, the following command

	perltidy -html somefile.pl

will produce a syntax-colored html file named F<somefile.pl.html>
which may be viewed with a browser.

B<Please Note>: In this case, perltidy does not do any formatting to the
input file, and it does not write a formatted file with extension
F<.tdy>.  This means that two perltidy runs are required to create a
fully reformatted, html copy of a script.  

=item  The B<-pre> flag for code snippets

When the B<-pre> flag is given, only the pre-formatted section, within
the <PRE> and </PRE> tags, will be output.  This simplifies inclusion
of the output in other files.  The default is to output a complete
web page.

=item  The B<-nnn> flag for line numbering

When the B<-nnn> flag is given, the output lines will be numbered.

=item  The B<-toc>, or B<--html-table-of-contents> flag

By default, a table of contents to packages and subroutines will be
written at the start of html output.  Use B<-ntoc> to prevent this.
This might be useful, for example, for a pod document which contains a
number of unrelated code snippets.  This flag only influences the code
table of contents; it has no effect on any table of contents produced by
pod2html (see next item).

=item  The B<-pod>, or B<--pod2html> flag

There are two options for formatting pod documentation.  The default is
to pass the pod through the Pod::Html module (which forms the basis of
the pod2html utility).  Any code sections are formatted by perltidy, and
the results then merged.  Note: perltidy creates a temporary file when
Pod::Html is used; see L<"FILES">.  Also, Pod::Html creates temporary
files for its cache.

NOTE: Perltidy counts the number of C<=cut> lines, and either moves the
pod text to the top of the html file if there is one C<=cut>, or leaves
the pod text in its original order (interleaved with code) otherwise.

Most of the flags accepted by pod2html may be included in the perltidy
command line, and they will be passed to pod2html.  In some cases,
the flags have a prefix C<pod> to emphasize that they are for the
pod2html, and this prefix will be removed before they are passed to
pod2html.  The flags which have the additional C<pod> prefix are:

   --[no]podheader --[no]podindex --[no]podrecurse --[no]podquiet 
   --[no]podverbose --podflush

The flags which are unchanged from their use in pod2html are:

   --backlink=s --cachedir=s --htmlroot=s --libpods=s --title=s
   --podpath=s --podroot=s 

where 's' is an appropriate character string.  Not all of these flags are
available in older versions of Pod::Html.  See your Pod::Html documentation for
more information.

The alternative, indicated with B<-npod>, is not to use Pod::Html, but
rather to format pod text in italics (or whatever the stylesheet
indicates), without special html markup.  This is useful, for example,
if pod is being used as an alternative way to write comments.

=item  The B<-frm>, or B<--frames> flag

By default, a single html output file is produced.  This can be changed
with the B<-frm> option, which creates a frame holding a table of
contents in the left panel and the source code in the right side. This
simplifies code browsing.  Assume, for example, that the input file is
F<MyModule.pm>.  Then, for default file extension choices, these three
files will be created:

 MyModule.pm.html      - the frame
 MyModule.pm.toc.html  - the table of contents
 MyModule.pm.src.html  - the formatted source code

Obviously this file naming scheme requires that output be directed to a real
file (as opposed to, say, standard output).  If this is not the
case, or if the file extension is unknown, the B<-frm> option will be
ignored.

=item  The B<-text=s>, or B<--html-toc-extension> flag

Use this flag to specify the extra file extension of the table of contents file
when html frames are used.  The default is "toc".
See L<Specifying File Extensions>.

=item  The B<-sext=s>, or B<--html-src-extension> flag

Use this flag to specify the extra file extension of the content file when html
frames are used.  The default is "src".
See L<Specifying File Extensions>.

=item  The B<-hent>, or B<--html-entities> flag

This flag controls the use of Html::Entities for html formatting.  By
default, the module Html::Entities is used to encode special symbols.
This may not be the right thing for some browser/language
combinations.  Use --nohtml-entities or -nhent to prevent this.

=item  Style Sheets

Style sheets make it very convenient to control and adjust the
appearance of html pages.  The default behavior is to write a page of
html with an embedded style sheet.

An alternative to an embedded style sheet is to create a page with a
link to an external style sheet.  This is indicated with the
B<-css=filename>,  where the external style sheet is F<filename>.  The
external style sheet F<filename> will be created if and only if it does
not exist.  This option is useful for controlling multiple pages from a
single style sheet.

To cause perltidy to write a style sheet to standard output and exit,
use the B<-ss>, or B<--stylesheet>, flag.  This is useful if the style
sheet could not be written for some reason, such as if the B<-pre> flag
was used.  Thus, for example,
  
  perltidy -html -ss >mystyle.css

will write a style sheet with the default properties to file
F<mystyle.css>.

The use of style sheets is encouraged, but a web page without a style
sheets can be created with the flag B<-nss>.  Use this option if you
must to be sure that older browsers (roughly speaking, versions prior to
4.0 of Netscape Navigator and Internet Explorer) can display the
syntax-coloring of the html files.

=item  Controlling HTML properties

Note: It is usually more convenient to accept the default properties
and then edit the stylesheet which is produced.  However, this section
shows how to control the properties with flags to perltidy.

Syntax colors may be changed from their default values by flags of the either
the long form, B<-html-color-xxxxxx=n>, or more conveniently the short form,
B<-hcx=n>, where B<xxxxxx> is one of the following words, and B<x> is the
corresponding abbreviation:

      Token Type             xxxxxx           x 
      ----------             --------         --
      comment                comment          c
      number                 numeric          n
      identifier             identifier       i
      bareword, function     bareword         w
      keyword                keyword          k
      quite, pattern         quote            q
      here doc text          here-doc-text    h
      here doc target        here-doc-target  hh
      punctuation            punctuation      pu
      parentheses            paren            p
      structural braces      structure        s
      semicolon              semicolon        sc
      colon                  colon            co
      comma                  comma            cm
      label                  label            j
      sub definition name    subroutine       m
      pod text               pod-text         pd

A default set of colors has been defined, but they may be changed by providing
values to any of the following parameters, where B<n> is either a 6 digit 
hex RGB color value or an ascii name for a color, such as 'red'.

To illustrate, the following command will produce an html 
file F<somefile.pl.html> with "aqua" keywords:

	perltidy -html -hck=00ffff somefile.pl

and this should be equivalent for most browsers:

	perltidy -html -hck=aqua somefile.pl

Perltidy merely writes any non-hex names that it sees in the html file.
The following 16 color names are defined in the HTML 3.2 standard:

	black   => 000000,
	silver  => c0c0c0,
	gray    => 808080,
	white   => ffffff,
	maroon  => 800000,
	red     => ff0000,
	purple  => 800080,
	fuchsia => ff00ff,
	green   => 008000,
	lime    => 00ff00,
	olive   => 808000,
	yellow  => ffff00
	navy    => 000080,
	blue    => 0000ff,
	teal    => 008080,
	aqua    => 00ffff,

Many more names are supported in specific browsers, but it is safest
to use the hex codes for other colors.  Helpful color tables can be
located with an internet search for "HTML color tables". 

Besides color, two other character attributes may be set: bold, and italics.
To set a token type to use bold, use the flag
B<--html-bold-xxxxxx> or B<-hbx>, where B<xxxxxx> or B<x> are the long
or short names from the above table.  Conversely, to set a token type to 
NOT use bold, use B<--nohtml-bold-xxxxxx> or B<-nhbx>.

Likewise, to set a token type to use an italic font, use the flag
B<--html-italic-xxxxxx> or B<-hix>, where again B<xxxxxx> or B<x> are the
long or short names from the above table.  And to set a token type to
NOT use italics, use B<--nohtml-italic-xxxxxx> or B<-nhix>.

For example, to use bold braces and lime color, non-bold, italics keywords the
following command would be used:

	perltidy -html -hbs -hck=00FF00 -nhbk -hik somefile.pl

The background color can be specified with B<--html-color-background=n>,
or B<-hcbg=n> for short, where n is a 6 character hex RGB value.  The
default color of text is the value given to B<punctuation>, which is
black as a default.

Here are some notes and hints:

1. If you find a preferred set of these parameters, you may want
to create a F<.perltidyrc> file containing them.  See the perltidy man
page for an explanation.

2. Rather than specifying values for these parameters, it is probably
easier to accept the defaults and then edit a style sheet.  The style
sheet contains comments which should make this easy.

3. The syntax-colored html files can be very large, so it may be best to
split large files into smaller pieces to improve download times.

=back

=head1 SOME COMMON INPUT CONVENTIONS

=head2 Specifying Block Types

Several parameters which refer to code block types may be customized by also
specifying an associated list of block types.  The type of a block is the name
of the keyword which introduces that block, such as B<if>, B<else>, or B<sub>.
An exception is a labeled block, which has no keyword, and should be specified
with just a colon.

For example, the following parameter specifies C<sub>, labels, C<BEGIN>, and
C<END> blocks:

   -cscl="sub : BEGIN END"

(the meaning of the -cscl parameter is described above.)  Note that
quotes are required around the list of block types because of the
spaces.

=head2 Specifying File Extensions

Several parameters allow default file extensions to be overridden.  For
example, a backup file extension may be specified with B<-bext=ext>,
where B<ext> is some new extension.  In order to provides the user some
flexibility, the following convention is used in all cases to decide if
a leading '.' should be used.  If the extension C<ext> begins with
C<A-Z>, C<a-z>, or C<0-9>, then it will be appended to the filename with
an intermediate '.' (or perhaps an '_' on VMS systems).  Otherwise, it
will be appended directly.  

For example, suppose the file is F<somefile.pl>.  For C<-bext=old>, a '.' is
added to give F<somefile.pl.old>.  For C<-bext=.old>, no additional '.' is
added, so again the backup file is F<somefile.pl.old>.  For C<-bext=~>, then no
dot is added, and the backup file will be F<somefile.pl~>  .  

=head1 SWITCHES WHICH MAY BE NEGATED

The following list shows all short parameter names which allow a prefix
'n' to produce the negated form:

 D    anl asc  aws  b    bbb bbc bbs  bl   bli  boc bok  bol  bot  ce
 csc  dac dbc  dcsc ddf  dln dnl dop  dp   dpro dsc dsm  dsn  dtt  dwls
 dwrs dws f    fll  frm  fs  hsc html ibc  icb  icp iob  isbc lal  log
 lp   lsl ohbr okw  ola  oll opr opt  osbr otr  ple ple  pod  pvl  q
 sbc  sbl schb scp  scsb sct se  sfp  sfs  skp  sob sohb sop  sosb sot
 ssc  st  sts  syn  t    tac tbc toc  tp   tqw  tsc w    x

Equivalently, the prefix 'no' or 'no-' on the corresponding long names may be
used.

=head1 LIMITATIONS

=over 4

=item  Parsing Limitations

Perltidy should work properly on most perl scripts.  It does a lot of
self-checking, but still, it is possible that an error could be
introduced and go undetected.  Therefore, it is essential to make
careful backups and to test reformatted scripts.

The main current limitation is that perltidy does not scan modules
included with 'use' statements.  This makes it necessary to guess the
context of any bare words introduced by such modules.  Perltidy has good
guessing algorithms, but they are not infallible.  When it must guess,
it leaves a message in the log file.

If you encounter a bug, please report it.

=item  What perltidy does not parse and format

Perltidy indents but does not reformat comments and C<qw> quotes. 
Perltidy does not in any way modify the contents of here documents or
quoted text, even if they contain source code.  (You could, however,
reformat them separately).  Perltidy does not format 'format' sections
in any way.  And, of course, it does not modify pod documents.

=back

=head1 FILES

=over 4

=item Temporary files

Under the -html option with the default --pod2html flag, a temporary file is
required to pass text to Pod::Html.  Unix systems will try to use the POSIX
tmpnam() function.  Otherwise the file F<perltidy.TMP> will be temporarily
created in the current working directory.

=item Special files when standard input is used

When standard input is used, the log file, if saved, is F<perltidy.LOG>,
and any errors are written to F<perltidy.ERR> unless the B<-se> flag is
set.  These are saved in the current working directory.  

=item Files overwritten

The following file extensions are used by perltidy, and files with these
extensions may be overwritten or deleted: F<.ERR>, F<.LOG>, F<.TEE>,
and/or F<.tdy>, F<.html>, and F<.bak>, depending on the run type and
settings.

=item  Files extensions limitations

Perltidy does not operate on files for which the run could produce a file with
a duplicated file extension.  These extensions include F<.LOG>, F<.ERR>,
F<.TEE>, and perhaps F<.tdy> and F<.bak>, depending on the run type.  The
purpose of this rule is to prevent generating confusing filenames such as
F<somefile.tdy.tdy.tdy>.

=back

=head1 SEE ALSO

perlstyle(1), Perl::Tidy(3)

#phoneticize
#!/usr/bin/perl

use String::Nysiis qw(nysiis);
use Text::Soundex;
use Getopt::Long;
use strict;

my @nysiis;
my @soundex;

my $result = GetOptions("nysiis=s" => \@nysiis,
                        "soundex=s" => \@soundex,
                       );

foreach my $raw_word (@nysiis) {
  my $phoneticized_word = nysiis($raw_word);
  print "$raw_word: $phoneticized_word (Nysiis)\n";
}

foreach my $raw_word (@soundex) {
  my $phoneticized_word = soundex($raw_word);
  print "$raw_word: $phoneticized_word (Soundex)\n";
}

#pod_cover
#!/usr/bin/perl -w

eval 'exec /usr/bin/perl -w -S $0 ${1+"$@"}'
    if 0; # not running under some shell

# Run this to get a coverage analysis of the embedded documentation

use Pod::Coverage;
use lib 'lib';			# to test distribution inside './lib'
use strict;

print "Pod coverage analysis v1.00 (C) by Tels 2001.\n";
print "Using Pod::Coverage v$Pod::Coverage::VERSION\n\n";

print scalar localtime()," Starting analysis:\n\n";

my $covered = 0; my $uncovered; my $count = 0; my $c;
open FILE, 'MANIFEST' or die "Can't read MANIFEST: $!";
while (<FILE>)
  {
  chomp;
  my ($file) = split /[\s\t]/,$_;
  next unless $file =~ /^lib.*\.pm$/;
  $file =~ s/^lib\///;			# remove lib and .pm
  $file =~ s/\.pm$//;
  $file =~ s/\//::/g;			# / => ::
  my $rc = Pod::Coverage->new( package => $file );
  $covered += $rc->covered(); 
  $uncovered += $rc->uncovered(); 
  $count ++;
  $c = $rc->coverage() || 0; 
  $c = int($c * 10000)/100;
  print "$file has a doc coverage of $c%.\n";
  my @naked = $rc->naked();
  if (@naked > 0)
    {
    print "Uncovered routines are:\n";
    print " ",join("\n ",sort @naked),"\n";	# sort by name
						# could sort by line_num
    }
  print "\n";
  }

my $total = $covered+$uncovered;
my $average = 'unknown';
$average = int(10000*$covered/$total)/100 if $total > 0;

print "Summary:\n";
print " sub routines total    : $total\n";
print " sub routines covered  : $covered\n";
print " sub routines uncovered: $uncovered\n";
print " total coverage        : $average%\n\n";

$current_process = $$;

$LOG_FILE = "$LOG_DIR/${NOW}.process_incoming.${current_process}.log";

if (! open(LOG, "> $LOG_FILE")) {
	print STDERR "ERROR: Cannot create log file $LOG_FILE : $!\n";
	&my_exit(1);
} else {
	print LOG "Log file: $LOG_FILE\n";

getopts('m:f:t:u:p:e:r:');

Process info on existing process follows:
$other_process_text\n");
	&my_exit(5);
}


$curr_time = time;

	$RUN_BEGIN_MONTH = $opt_t;

	if (defined($opt_u)) {

}

sub my_exit() {
	my($exit_code) = shift;

	if (-f $LOG_FILE) {
		close(LOG);
	}

	&cleanup_log;

	if ($exit_code != 0) {
		if (-f $LOG_FILE) {
			if (defined($email_list)) {
				system("mailx -s 'process_incoming failure' $email_list < $LOG_FILE");
			}
		} else {
			if (defined($email_list)) {
				system("echo 'No logging details available' | mailx -s 'process_incoming failure' $email_list");
			}
		}
	} else {
		# remove log file if no errors and no meaningful activity happened

		$ret = system("egrep -i 'Files moved: *[^0]|Files sent: *[^0]|c2 file generated:|mmi_ub file successfully generated:|nsf_clean file successfully generated:' $LOG_FILE > /dev/null");
		$ret = $ret >> 8;

		if ($ret != 0) {
			unlink($LOG_FILE);
		}
	}

	exit($exit_code);
}

sub log_mesg() {
	print LOG $_[0];
	print STDERR $_[0];
}

if ($num_prog_args <= 0) {
	print "Usage: $0 [-m move_sources_list] [-f ftp_id_list] [-t c2_gen_YYYYMM] [-r run_id_list] [-p ftp_YYYYMM] [-e email_list] [-t YYYYMM [-u YYYYMM]]\n";
	print "	ftp_id_list (comma-seperated list)	Valid values: " . join(' ', keys %PROD_SEND) . "\n";
	print "	move_sources_list (comma-seperated list)	Valid values: " . join(' ', keys %MOVE_SOURCES) . "\n";
	print "	run_id_list (comma-seperated list)	Valid values: " . join(' ', keys %{$RUN}) . "\n";
	print "	-t	Beginning month for -r run_id_list (defaults to previous month if not specified)\n";
	print "	-u	Ending month for -r run_id_list (defaults to -t value if not specified, or current month if -t not specified)\n";


	&my_exit(1);
}

sub get_yyyymm() {

	($sec,$min,$hour,$mday,$mon,$year,$wday,$yday,$isdst) = localtime(shift);

	return sprintf('%4d%02d', $year + 1900, $mon + 1);
}

@LOG_IGNORE_TEXT = split("\n",
"Property of NDCHealth
########################### NOTICE from ndcHEALTH #############################
Red Hat Enterprise Linux ES release 3
###############################################################################
This system is for the use of authorized users only.  Individuals using this
computer system without authority, or in excess of their authority, are subject
to having all of their activities on this system monitored and recorded by
system personnel.
In the course of monitoring individuals improperly using this system, or in the
course of system maintenance, the activities of authorized users may also be
monitored.
The use of this system constitues consent by the user to the monitoring
described above.  If as a result of this monitoring improper or illegal
activities are identified NDCHealth will take appropriate action up to and
including the reporting of such to the appropriate government officials."
);

sub cleanup_log() {

  my($TEMP_LOG, $log_line, $ret);

	$TEMP_LOG = "${LOG_FILE}.temp";

	close(LOG);
	open(LOG_READ, $LOG_FILE) || return 0;
	open(LOG_WRITE, "> ${TEMP_LOG}") || return 0;

	LOG_LINE:
	while (<LOG_READ>) {
		$log_line = $_;
		chop($log_line);

		foreach $ignore_line (@LOG_IGNORE_TEXT) {
			if ( ($log_line =~ /^${ignore_line}/) or ($log_line =~ /^\s*$/) ) {
				next LOG_LINE;
			}
		}

		if (! print LOG_WRITE $log_line . "\n") {
			close(LOG_WRITE);
			close(LOG_READ);
			unlink($TEMP_LOG);
			return 0;
		}
	}

	close(LOG_WRITE);
	close(LOG_READ);

	$ret = system('mv', $TEMP_LOG, $LOG_FILE);
	$ret = $ret >> 8;

	if ($ret != 0) {
		unlink($TEMP_LOG);
		return 0;
	} else {
		return 1;
	}
}

sub do_system() {
  my($ret);

	close(LOG);

	$ret = system(join(' ', @_) . " >> $LOG_FILE 2>&1");
	$ret = $? >> 8;

	if (! open(LOG, ">> $LOG_FILE")) {
		print STDERR "ERROR: Cannot create log file $LOG_FILE : $!\n";
        	&my_exit(1);
	}

	return $ret;
}


if (defined($opt_m)) {
	foreach $source (split(',', $opt_m)) {
		$temp_source = $MOVE_SOURCES{$source};
		$temp_source_list{$temp_source} = 1;
	}

	foreach $temp_source (keys %temp_source_list) {
		push(@source_list, $temp_source);
	}

	foreach $source (@source_list) {
#		print "debug: " . join(' ', 'move_sources', '-o', '-a', '-s', $source) . "\n";

		if (&do_system('move_sources', '-o', '-a', '-s', $source) != 0) {
			&log_mesg("ERROR: move_sources failed for source $source\n");
			$move_sources_failures++;
		} else {
			$move_sources_successes++;
		}
	}

	if ($move_sources_failures > 0) {
		&log_mesg("ERROR: move_sources failed $move_sources_failures time(s)\n");
		&log_mesg("Note: move_sources succeeded $move_sources_successes times(s)\n");
	}

	if ($move_sources_successes == 0) {
		&log_mesg("ERROR: No completely successful executions of move_sources\n");
		&my_exit(1);
	}
}


# run other commands to generate deliverables

foreach $run_id (@run_id_list) {

	if ($RUN->{$run_id}->{work_unit_source} eq 'gen_wu') {

		if ((exists($RUN->{$run_id}->{command_success_exit})) and (defined($RUN->{$run_id}->{command_success_exit}))) {
			$command_success_exit = $RUN->{$run_id}->{command_success_exit};
		} else {
			$command_success_exit = 0;
		}

		$ret = system('gen_wu -t ' . $RUN->{$run_id}->{work_unit_info}->{TYPE} . ' -v ' . $RUN->{$run_id}->{work_unit_info}->{VERSION} . ' -s ' . $RUN->{$run_id}->{work_unit_info}->{SOURCES} . ' ' . $RUN->{$run_id}->{work_unit_info}->{BEGIN_MONTH} . ' ' . $RUN->{$run_id}->{work_unit_info}->{END_MONTH} . " | prun2 -e $command_success_exit -r $PROCESS_HOST_LIST " . $RUN->{$run_id}->{command} . " >> $LOG_FILE 2>&1");
		$ret = $ret >> 8;

		if ($ret != 0) {
			&log_mesg("ERROR: prun2 failed for at least one $run_id command " . $RUN->{$run_id}->{command} . "\n");
			$run_failures++;
		}

	}

}

# prod_send -c prod_send_configfile -i id

if (defined($opt_f)) {
	@prod_send_id_list = split(',', $opt_f);
}

if ($#prod_send_id_list >= 0) {

	if (! -f $PROD_SEND_CONFIG_FILE) {
		&log_mesg("ERROR: prod_send config file $PROD_SEND_CONFIG_FILE does not exist!\n");
		&my_exit(1);
	}

	foreach $id (@prod_send_id_list) {

		$type = $PROD_SEND{$id}{'TYPE'};

		if ($type =~ /^UB|^NSF/i) {
			$sources = $PROD_SEND{$id}{'SOURCES'};
			$begin_month = $PROD_SEND{$id}{'BEGIN_MONTH'};
			$end_month = $PROD_SEND{$id}{'END_MONTH'};
			$version = $PROD_SEND{$id}{'VERSION'};

			@PS_FILES = `gen_wu -w -e -t $type -v $version -s $sources $begin_month $end_month`;

			$ret = $? >> 8;

			if ($ret != 0) {
				&log_mesg("ERROR: gen_wu failed for -w -t $type -v $version -s $sources $begin_month $end_month\n");
				&my_exit(1);
			}

			for($ind = 0; $ind <= $#PS_FILES; $ind++) {
				chomp($PS_FILES[$ind]);
			}

		} elsif ($type =~ /custom/i) {

			$source_dir = $PROD_SEND{$id}{SOURCE_DIR};
			$file_glob = $PROD_SEND{$id}{FILE_GLOB};

#			if ($PROD_SEND{$id}{PASSIVE}) {
#				$passive = '-p';
#			} else {
#				$passive = '';
#			}

			@PS_FILES = glob("$source_dir/$file_glob");

		} else {
			&log_mesg("ERROR: Don't understand PROD_SEND type of '$type'. Only types supported are NSF, UB, or CUSTOM\n");
			&my_exit(1);
		}

		# Moved passive check outside of if/elsif - 
    # was being set for mmub (type custom) and not reset for tulsa_clear_hcfa (type NSF)
		# should not affect type nsf/ub - 
		# will set $passive to '' if they don't have the PASSIVE hash key set 
		if ($PROD_SEND{$id}{PASSIVE}) {
			$passive = '-p';
		} else {
			$passive = '';
		}

		if (($#PS_FILES < 0) or (! -f $PS_FILES[0])) {
			next;
		}

#print STDERR "debug: Calling prod_send $passive -c $PROD_SEND_CONFIG_FILE -i $id ..." . $PROD_SEND{$id}{PASSIVE} . "...\n";

		if (! open(PS, "| prod_send $passive -c $PROD_SEND_CONFIG_FILE -i $id >> $LOG_FILE 2>&1")) {
			&log_mesg("ERROR: Unable to launch prod_send for id $id: $!\n");
			&my_exit(1);
		}

		foreach $fname (@PS_FILES) {

#print STDERR "debug: sending to prod_send: $fname\n";

			if (! print PS $fname . "\n") {
				&log_mesg("ERROR: Unable to send file list to prod_send for id $id : $!\n");
				&my_exit(1);
			}
		}

		close(PS);

		$ret = $? >> 8;

		if ($ret > 0) {
			&log_mesg("ERROR: At least one file failed to transfer\n");
			$prod_send_failures++;
		}
	}
}

if ($move_sources_failures + $c2_gen_failures + $prod_send_failures + $run_failures > 0) {

	&log_mesg("move_sources failures: $move_sources_failures\n");
	&log_mesg("c2_gen_failures: $c2_gen_failures\n");
	&log_mesg("prod_send_failures: $prod_send_failures\n");
	&log_mesg("run_failures: $run_failures\n");
	&log_mesg("Log file: $LOG_FILE\n");

	&my_exit(80);
}

&my_exit(0);


#prod_send
#!/usr/bin/perl

use Getopt::Std;

our $DS_BASE_DIR = $ENV{DS_BASE_DIR};
die "ERROR: DS_BASE_DIR environment variable is '$DS_BASE_DIR', which is not an existing directory\n" if (! ((defined($DS_BASE_DIR)) && (-d $DS_BASE_DIR)));

$bftp_config_file = "$DS_BASE_DIR/common/etc/config_prod_send.bftp";

if ($#ARGV < 0) {
	print "Usage: $0 -c prod_send_configfile -i id [-p] [-b bftp_configfile]\n";
	exit(0);
}

getopts('c:i:b:p');

if (defined($opt_p)) {
	$passive_option = '-p';
} else {
	$passive_option = '';
}

if (defined($opt_c)) {
	$ps_config_file = $opt_c;
} else {
	die "ERROR: Must specify -c prod_send_configfile option\n";
}

if (! -f $ps_config_file) {
	die "ERROR: prod_send_configfile $ps_config_file does not exist\n";
}

if (defined($opt_b)) {
	$bftp_config_file = $opt_b;
}

if (! -f $bftp_config_file) {
	die "ERROR: bftp_configfile $bftp_config_file does not exist\n";
}

if (defined($opt_i)) {
	$id = $opt_i;
} else {
	die "ERROR: Must specify -i id option\n";
}

if (length($id) <= 0) {
	die "ERROR: Must specify non-empty -i id option\n";
}

sub read_ps_config() {
  my($ps_config_file) = shift;

	open(PS_CONFIG, $ps_config_file) || die "ERROR: Could not open prod_send_configfile $ps_config_file : $!\n";

	while (<PS_CONFIG>) {
		chop;

		# skip blank lines and comment lines
		next if /^\s*$/;
		next if /^\s*#/;

		$original_line = $_;

		($line_id, $host, $username, $password, $dir, $line_newest_file_sent, $line_file_mtime) = split(',', $original_line);

		if (length($line_id) == 0) {
			print STDERR "Warning: First field of prod_send_configfile $ps_config_file is blank: $original_line\n";
		} else {

			if ($dir eq '') {
				$dir = '.';
			}

			if (($line_file_mtime =~ /^\s*$/) and (-f $line_newest_file_sent)) {
				($dev,$ino,$mode,$nlink,$uid,$gid,$rdev,$file_size,$atime,$line_file_mtime,$ctime,$blksize,$blocks) = stat($line_newest_file_sent);
			}

			$PS_CONFIG{$line_id}{'HOST'} = $host;
			$PS_CONFIG{$line_id}{'USERNAME'} = $username;
			$PS_CONFIG{$line_id}{'PASSWORD'} = $password;
			$PS_CONFIG{$line_id}{'DIR'} = $dir;
			$PS_CONFIG{$line_id}{'NEWEST_FILE_NAME'} = $line_newest_file_sent;
			$PS_CONFIG{$line_id}{'NEWEST_FILE_MTIME'} = $line_file_mtime;
		}
	}

	close(PS_CONFIG);
}

&read_ps_config($ps_config_file);

if (! (exists($PS_CONFIG{$id}))) {
	die "Unable to find id of $id in prod_send_configfile $ps_config_file\n";
}

$previous_newest_file_mtime = $PS_CONFIG{$id}{NEWEST_FILE_MTIME};
$previous_newest_file_name = $PS_CONFIG{$id}{NEWEST_FILE_NAME};

if ($previous_newest_file_mtime eq '') {
	$previous_newest_file_mtime = 0;
}

$current_newest_file_mtime = $previous_newest_file_mtime;

if ($DEBUG) {
	print STDERR "Previous newest file name = $previous_newest_file_name\n";
}

while (<STDIN>) {
	chop;

	next if /^\s*$/;

	$send_fname = $_;

	$send_fname_dir = $send_fname;

	if ($send_fname_dir =~ /\//) {
		$send_fname_dir =~ s!/[^/]+$!!;
	} else {
		$send_fname_dir = $ENV{PWD};
	}

	$send_fname_basename = $send_fname;
	$send_fname_basename =~ s!^.*/([^/]+)$!$1!;

	if ($send_fname_basename eq '') {
		$send_fname_basename = $send_fname;
	}

	$reconstructed_fname = $send_fname_dir . '/' . $send_fname_basename;

	if (! -f $reconstructed_fname) {
		print STDERR "ERROR: Reconstructed full pathname of file $reconstructed_fname does not exist!\n";
		$failed_files++;
		next;
	}

	($dev,$ino,$mode,$nlink,$uid,$gid,$rdev,$file_size,$atime,$mtime,$ctime,$blksize,$blocks) = stat($reconstructed_fname);

	if ($mtime > $previous_newest_file_mtime) {
		$temp_file_list{$mtime}{$reconstructed_fname} = 1;
	}
}


# populate file send list in order of mtime (oldest to newest)
$i = 0;

foreach $mtime (sort { $a <=> $b } keys %temp_file_list) {
	foreach $fname (keys %{$temp_file_list{$mtime}}) {
		$files_to_send[$i]{'NAME'} = $fname;
		$files_to_send[$i]{'MTIME'} = $mtime;
		$i++;
	}
}

$ps_config_file_temp = $ps_config_file . '.temp';

for($i = 0; $i <= $#files_to_send; $i++) {
	$send_fname = $files_to_send[$i]{'NAME'};
	$mtime = $files_to_send[$i]{'MTIME'};


	$send_fname_dir = $send_fname;

	if ($send_fname_dir =~ /\//) {
		$send_fname_dir =~ s!/[^/]+$!!;
	} else {
		$send_fname_dir = $ENV{PWD};
	}

	$send_fname_basename = $send_fname;
	$send_fname_basename =~ s!^.*/([^/]+)$!$1!;

	if ($send_fname_basename eq '') {
		$send_fname_basename = $send_fname;
	}

	print STDERR "Attempting to send file $send_fname\n";

	$ENV{PROD_SEND_PASS} = $PS_CONFIG{$id}{PASSWORD};

	print STDERR "debug: bftp.pl -f $bftp_config_file $passive_option -v FILE=$send_fname_basename,HOST=$PS_CONFIG{$id}{HOST},SOURCE_DIR=$send_fname_dir,USER=$PS_CONFIG{$id}{USERNAME},DEST_DIR=$PS_CONFIG{$id}{DIR},ID=$id\n";

	$ret = system("bftp.pl -f $bftp_config_file $passive_option -v FILE=$send_fname_basename,HOST=$PS_CONFIG{$id}{HOST},SOURCE_DIR=$send_fname_dir,USER=$PS_CONFIG{$id}{USERNAME},DEST_DIR=$PS_CONFIG{$id}{DIR},ID=$id");

	#$ret = system('bftp.pl', '-f', $bftp_config_file, '-v', "FILE=$send_fname_basename,HOST=$PS_CONFIG{$id}{HOST},SOURCE_DIR=$send_fname_dir,USER=$PS_CONFIG{$id}{USERNAME},DEST_DIR=$PS_CONFIG{$id}{DIR},ID=$id");

	$ret = $ret >> 8;

	if ($ret != 0) {
		print STDERR "ERROR: Could not send file $send_fname\n";
		$failed_files++;
		next;
	}

	push(@sent_files, $send_fname);

	$PS_CONFIG{$id}{'NEWEST_FILE_NAME'} = $send_fname;
	$PS_CONFIG{$id}{'NEWEST_FILE_MTIME'} = $mtime;

	open(PS_CONFIG_TEMP, "> $ps_config_file_temp") || die "ERROR: Unable to create temp copy of prodsend_config file $ps_config_file as $ps_config_file_temp : $!\n";

	foreach $config_id (sort keys %PS_CONFIG) {
		print(	PS_CONFIG_TEMP join(',',
			$config_id,
			$PS_CONFIG{$config_id}{'HOST'},
			$PS_CONFIG{$config_id}{'USERNAME'},
			$PS_CONFIG{$config_id}{'PASSWORD'},
			$PS_CONFIG{$config_id}{'DIR'},
			$PS_CONFIG{$config_id}{'NEWEST_FILE_NAME'},
			$PS_CONFIG{$config_id}{'NEWEST_FILE_MTIME'}
		) . "\n") || die "ERROR: Unable to create temp copy of prodsend_config file $ps_config_file : $!\n";

	}

	close(PS_CONFIG_TEMP);

	$ret = system('mv', $ps_config_file_temp, $ps_config_file);
	$ret = $ret >> 8;

	if ($ret != 0) {
		die "ERROR: Unable to rename temp copy of $ps_config_file_temp to $ps_config_file\n";
	}

	$files_sent++;
}


if ($files_sent > 0) {
	print STDERR "Files sent: $files_sent $id to $PS_CONFIG{$id}{HOST}:\n";
	print STDERR join("\n", @sent_files) . "\n";
}

if ($failed_files > 0) {
	print STDERR "$failed_files $id files failed to transfer to $PS_CONFIG{$id}{HOST}\n";
	exit(10);
} else {
	if ($PS_CONFIG{$id}{'NEWEST_FILE_MTIME'} == $previous_newest_file_mtime) {
		print STDERR "No new $id files to send\n";
		exit(0);
	}

	exit(0);
}

cd_func ()
{
  local x2 the_new_dir adir index
  local -i cnt

  if [[ $1 ==  "--" ]]; then
    dirs -v
    return 0
  fi

  the_new_dir=$1
  [[ -z $1 ]] && the_new_dir=$HOME

  if [[ ${the_new_dir:0:1} == '-' ]]; then
    #
    # Extract dir N from dirs
    index=${the_new_dir:1}
    [[ -z $index ]] && index=1
    adir=$(dirs +$index)
    [[ -z $adir ]] && return 1
    the_new_dir=$adir
  fi

  #
  # '~' has to be substituted by ${HOME}
  [[ ${the_new_dir:0:1} == '~' ]] && the_new_dir="${HOME}${the_new_dir:1}"

  #
  # Now change to the new dir and add to the top of the stack
  pushd "${the_new_dir}" > /dev/null
  [[ $? -ne 0 ]] && return 1
  the_new_dir=$(pwd)

  #
  # Trim down everything beyond 11th entry
  popd -n +11 2>/dev/null 1>/dev/null

  #
  # Remove any other occurence of this dir, skipping the top of the stack
  for ((cnt=1; cnt <= 10; cnt++)); do
    x2=$(dirs +${cnt} 2>/dev/null)
    [[ $? -ne 0 ]] && return 0
    [[ ${x2:0:1} == '~' ]] && x2="${HOME}${x2:1}"
    if [[ "${x2}" == "${the_new_dir}" ]]; then
      popd -n +$cnt 2>/dev/null 1>/dev/null
      cnt=cnt-1
    fi
  done

  return 0
}


DS_BASE_DIR=/ds

# Add sourcing of readable profiles 6/21/2011 - J Hess

profile_dir=$DS_BASE_DIR/common/profile
oldpwd=$PWD

if cd $profile_dir
  then
		for p in profile_*.bash
			do
				if [ ! -r $p ]
					then
						continue
				fi

				case $p in
					profile_$USER.bash)  user_script=$p
																continue;;
				esac

				if . $p; then
					profiles_sourced="$profiles_sourced $p"
				else
					profiles_failed="$profiles_failed $p"
				fi

			done

		if [ -r "$user_script" ]
			then
				if . $user_script; then
					profiles_sourced="$profiles_sourced $user_script"
				else
					profiles_failed="$profiles_failed $user_script"
				fi
		fi

		if [ "$profiles_failed" != '' ]; then
			echo >&2
			echo "- $BASE_DIR PROFILES UNABLE TO SOURCE!:$profiles_failed" >&2
		fi

		if [ -t 0 ]; then
			echo "- $BASE_DIR profiles sourced: $profiles_sourced"
		fi

		cd $oldpwd
  else
		echo "Could not cd to $profile_dir to source profiles!" >&2
fi

cd_func ()
{
  local x2 the_new_dir adir index
  local -i cnt

  if [[ $1 ==  "--" ]]; then
    dirs -v
    return 0
  fi

  the_new_dir=$1
  [[ -z $1 ]] && the_new_dir=$HOME

  if [[ ${the_new_dir:0:1} == '-' ]]; then
    #
    # Extract dir N from dirs
    index=${the_new_dir:1}
    [[ -z $index ]] && index=1
    adir=$(dirs +$index)
    [[ -z $adir ]] && return 1
    the_new_dir=$adir
  fi

  #
  # '~' has to be substituted by ${HOME}
  [[ ${the_new_dir:0:1} == '~' ]] && the_new_dir="${HOME}${the_new_dir:1}"

  #
  # Now change to the new dir and add to the top of the stack
  pushd "${the_new_dir}" > /dev/null
  [[ $? -ne 0 ]] && return 1
  the_new_dir=$(pwd)

  #
  # Trim down everything beyond 11th entry
  popd -n +11 2>/dev/null 1>/dev/null

  #
  # Remove any other occurence of this dir, skipping the top of the stack
  for ((cnt=1; cnt <= 10; cnt++)); do
    x2=$(dirs +${cnt} 2>/dev/null)
    [[ $? -ne 0 ]] && return 0
    [[ ${x2:0:1} == '~' ]] && x2="${HOME}${x2:1}"
    if [[ "${x2}" == "${the_new_dir}" ]]; then
      popd -n +$cnt 2>/dev/null 1>/dev/null
      cnt=cnt-1
    fi
  done

  return 0
}


DS_BASE_DIR=/ds

# Add sourcing of readable profiles 6/21/2011 - J Hess

profile_dir=$DS_BASE_DIR/common/profile
oldpwd=$PWD

if cd $profile_dir
  then
		for p in profile_*.bash
			do
				if [ ! -r $p ]
					then
						continue
				fi

				case $p in
					profile_$USER.bash)  user_script=$p
																continue;;
				esac

				if . $p; then
					profiles_sourced="$profiles_sourced $p"
				else
					profiles_failed="$profiles_failed $p"
				fi

			done

		if [ -r "$user_script" ]
			then
				if . $user_script; then
					profiles_sourced="$profiles_sourced $user_script"
				else
					profiles_failed="$profiles_failed $user_script"
				fi
		fi

		if [ "$profiles_failed" != '' ]; then
			echo >&2
			echo "- $BASE_DIR PROFILES UNABLE TO SOURCE!:$profiles_failed" >&2
		fi

		if [ -t 0 ]; then
			echo "- $BASE_DIR profiles sourced: $profiles_sourced"
		fi

		cd $oldpwd
  else
		echo "Could not cd to $profile_dir to source profiles!" >&2
fi

#prun3
#!/usr/bin/perl

# Program: prun2
#
# Run a command in parallel
#
# Author: jmh
#
# general syntax: prun2 [options] [--] cmd [options] [%p] [--] [arg1] [%p] [arg2] [...] 
# example syntax: prun2 [options] cmd [%p] [arg1] [%p] [arg2] [...] 
# example syntax: prun2 [options] -- cmd <cmd_options> [-cmd_opt %p] [%p] -- [arg1] [arg2] [...] 
# example syntax: prun2 [options] -- cmd <cmd_options> [%p] [arg1] [arg2] [...] 
#
# Example 1: run gzip 5 at a time, getting work units from command line arguments (*.dat)
# prun2 -p 5 gzip *.dat
#
# Example 2: same as #1, but get work units from workunit file
# prun2 -f workunit -p 5 gzip
#
# Example 3: same as #1, but get work units from standard input
# find . -name '*.dat' -print |  prun2 -p 5 gzip
#
# Example 4: same as #1, but passing -c option to gunzip
# prun2 -p 5 -- gunzip -c *.dat.gz
# (must use -- before gunzip to avoid confusion between prun2 options and gunzip options)
#
# Example 5: run "gzip" 6 at a time, with "-S .GZ option" passed to gzip, getting work units from command line arguments (*.dat)
# (must use -- before *.dat so prun2 won't mistakenly think that ".GZ" is one of the work units)
# prun2 -p 6 -- gzip -S .GZ -- *.dat
#
# Example 6: same as #4, with alternate syntax
# prun2 -p 6 -- gzip -S .GZ %p *.dat
# (any occurrance of %p is replaced by a work unit with each execution of gzip)
#
# Example 7: run "cmd" 6 at a time, passing "-s %p" work unit arguments as first argument to cmd, work units
# obtained from command line arguments (*.dat)
# prun2 -p 6 -- cmd -s %p -k -c *.dat

# options:
# -a failures: maximum # child process failures before main
# parent process will terminate
# -e exit_code : exit value representing "normal" exit from child processes
# (defaults to 0)
# -f todo_file : file containing list of parameters to pass to children
# -p threads : maximum # of threads (children) to run. Default = 1.
# (modifiable dynamically via todo_file.control file
# -h : Display program usage
# -l : Lower scheduling priority to 14 (Default unchanged)\n";
#
# 10/3/2002 : Removed false warning about inability to remove
# control file when work units aquired from STDIN
#
# 10/15/2002 : Added detection of unexpected lack of child processes to wait for
# 10/15/2002 : Fixed max_child_failures bug
#
# 10/17/2002 : Added usage display.
# 10/17/2002 : Added sanity checking to command line arguments and options.
# 10/17/2002 : Added ability to get work units from command line arguments
#
# 10/22/2002 : Added example executions to comments and usage
# 10/22/2002 : Added support for -h (help) option
# 10/22/2002 : Added support for changing scheduling priority (-l mimicks nice, -n # sets to specific nice value)
#
# 10/28/2002 : Changed reporting of max threads to current threads when writing to done file
#
# 02/11/2003 : Changed signal handler for abnormal termination so that it kill all running child processes
# instead of waiting for them to complete.
#
# 05/06/2003 : Added remaining time info to log info. Removed elapsed info from log.
#
# 6/9/2003 : Ignored SIGTTOU signal
# 6/9/2003 : Improved remaining time calc to account for elapsed time of currently executing child processes
#
# 11/18/2003 : Added ability to add servers via control file *after* launching prun
#
# 12/02/2003 : Added Remaining Items info to log output when work unit completes successfully
#
# 12/17/2003 : Added -m option for max # of work unit attempts (default 1). Only downside to this is
# that a failed work unit will not be retried until *after* all other work units have had a chance
# to be attempted (to completion or failure) the same number of times as itself. For example, if a work
# unit has failed once but there is still one work unit running its 1st attempt, the failed work unit
# will not be attempted a second time until the other work unit completes its first attempt.
#
#            : Enhanced initial and trailing log info
#
# 12/18/2003 : Server info data is now periodically refreshed from server.info file.
# This includes servers being added to and taken out of server groups. Server info file
# can be updated manually or automatically (by another process) on some periodic schedule.
#
# 1/16/2004 : Removed -s control_check_interval option. Modification time of control file is used to
# detect change to control file
# 1/16/2004 : Modification time of server info file is used to detect change to server info setup data
# 1/16/2004 : Added ability to append additional work units to work unit file
# 1/16/2004 : Fixed bug. Previous addition of that supported moving servers in and out of groups in server
# info file caused program to erroneously remove servers not in a group listed in server info file. Fixed.
#
# 2/23/2004 : Added -q option for quiet mode. This will prevent all but the most critical messages from being
# output to STDERR.
#
# 5/14/2004 : If work units are files, they will now be launched in descending file size order. This
# can decrease overall processing time by starting longer-running work units before shorter ones.
#
# 5/17/2004 : Added -t option, which prevents control file, work units, and done files from being removed
# when at least one work unit failed and -f option was NOT used.
#
# 6/2/2004 : Added sourcing of /etc/profile on remote server prior to execution of work unit. Only sourced
# if it exists. Previously, only $HOME/.profile was sourced.
#
# 7/2/2004 : Removed -p option, since it had become obsolete and could become problematic under certain
# circumstances.
# 7/2/2004 : Added requirement that work units be unique.
#
# 9/14/2004 : In remote shell command, fixed missing end quote issue that only caused problem when
# running from Linux.
#
# 9/16/2004 : Added support for naming server groups in control file
#
# 9/29/2004 : Added -j job_name option, for display in execution report
# 9/29/2004 : Added "work unit source" and "work unit range" display to execution report
#
# 10/08/2004 : Work unit specified by -f option no longer supports file names ending with '.done'
#
# 11/16/2004 : Added close(SI) after finished reading server info file. Suspected of causing problems
# on subsequent reads of server info file.
#
# 12/8/2004 : Fixed buggy behavior associated with control file and server info updates. Also
# simplified some of this logic.
#
# 12/9/2004 : Removed warning about mismatched work unit order when work units are files that were
# resorted in filesize order. Limitation: new work units added while running will be ignored if work units are files.
#
# 12/14/2004 : Fixed long-standing issue of remote work units (i.e. those not executing on same server as prun)
# not being killed when main prun process is killed.
#
# 12/22/2004 : Added current and elapsed time to log when work unit fails.
# - Moved current time to same line as work unit line in log file upon work unit success.
#
# 1/10/2006 : Added -b option to inhibit attempt to launch work units in descending file size order.
#
# 2/2/2006 : Removed -n option.
# - Changed -l option to cause command to be prefixed with "nice" command instead of calling setpriority
#
# 9/7/2006 : Changed -l option to launch workunits via "nice -n 14" instead of just "nice"
# - Added -p priority option to allow a specific priority (nice) value to be used to launch work units
# - Added ability to set or modify workunit nice values via "priority = #" setting in control file
# - Added common logging, which is turned on when LOG_DIR environment variable is present
#
# 9/19/2006 : Fixed bug where work units on command line would get appened to end of each command line executed
# (introduced in previous version)
#
# 9/20/2006 : Added support for alternate "server info" file locations
# Precedence is: command line option -v overrides environment variable PRUN2_SERVER_INFO,
#		environment variable overrides hard-coded default (currently /ds/common/etc/server.info)
#
# 10/4/2006 : prun2 exit code now based on number of remaining work units instead of
# checking for failed work units. This is because failed work units can be retried and
# subsequently succeed.
#
# 10/10/2006 : Enhanced child pid kill procedure so that a "kill"ed local child will only terminate
# AFTER it's associated remote child pid has actually died (i.e. now we do a kill every 10 seconds
# until the kill command gives an error, which means the pid no longer exists). Clever, indeed
# (albeit a bit tardy).
#
# - Also enhanced auto-removal of work units and done files so that it's only attempted if
# they were actually created.
#
# - Also removed file_exists() function, since it's no longer used.
#
# 10/17/2006 : Added 5 second delay between 1st and 2nd kill attempt when killing work units. This gives
# the work unit a decent amount of time to gracefully cleanup and exit instead of being hit/interrupted with
# 2 near-simultaneous kill signals. Also, as a result we should now see fewer
# "trying again to kill pid ..." messages from prun2.  This is a refinement of the kill enhancements
# added on 10/10/2006.
#
# 1/10/2007 : Changed $DEFAULT_SERVER_INFO_FILE to use $DS_BASE_DIR environment variable instead of
# hard-coded '/ds' value.
#
# 2/4/2007 : Changed chop() calls to chomp() calls.
#
# 5/18/2007 : Fixed bug where work units would not get launched on servers added to server.info file while
# prun2 is running.  This was in set_run_server_info().
#
# 8/8/2007 : Added -d temp_dir option, which allows specification of directory where prun2 will create
# temp work unit and done files when the -f option is not used.
#
# 3/31/2008 : Added date/time-stamp prefix to log message "Running on ....". Also removed "via ssh"
# from same log message.
#
# 8/1/2008 : Skip commented lines when reading control file in read_control_info() function
# (previously was only skipped in init)
#
# 8/4/2008 : work unit kills will now use "kill -9" after 4 failed attempts to kill the nice way
# Changed wait interval between kills from 10 to 15 seconds.
#
# 10/21/2008 : Added -x max_host_failures option, defaulting to 3. Host will be auto-removed
# after this number of successive failures on a server.
#
# 11/6/2008 : Enhanced parallel degree component of -r option. Can now optionally add percent
# character (e.g. -r rx:50%) to specify a percent of processors instead of a number of processors.
# More helpful for group specs than individual servers.
#
# 12/20/2008 : Added error detection and handling for when DONE file cannot be appended to upon
# successful work unit completion. No new work units will be launched after this happens.
#
# 1/14/2009 : Modified ssh/rsh child launcher code to stop reading from ssh file handle as soon
# as PRUN2_CHILD_RETURN_STATUS tag is found, instead of reading until handle is closed.
# This was done because *sometimes* sshd on the remote host will keep waiting (and therefore
# leave the handle open) indefinitely, even though the child command has completed.
# When that happens, the result may be an orphaned sshd process hanging around indefinitely,
# but that's better than also having a prun2 process that hangs around indefinitely despite child
# work units that actually did exit.
#
# 1/14/2009 : Added quiet switch (-q) to "ssh kill" command in remote_kill() function, to supress login banner
#
# 1/14/2009 : Fixed newline problem with "Killing all currently executing work units.." logging message in sig_handler() function.
#
# v 2.6 7/1/2010
#
# - Changed the way current directory is determined. Previously used cwd(), but that would
# return /dsmounts/{curr_dir} when AUTOFS is used on NFS clients instead of just {curr_dir}. Now it uses
# $ENV{PWD} if it exists, otherwise it uses cwd().
#
# v2.7 8/19/2011 : When -r option is not used, will look for host_spec in PRUN_PARALLEL_HOST_SPEC
# environment variable, but will revert to previous default of local host if it is not set.
#
# 6/x/2010 : MAJOR ENHANCEMENT - Added true load balancing capability
# Using server load monitoring daemons and "best server" chooser daemon via the Schedule::Load
# family of modules, get_available_server() was rewritten to provide real load-balancing
# capability. This necessitated other related changes, such as:
#
# 1) Changing blocking waits to non-blocking waits. This allows work units to be launched
# within a few seconds of available CPU cycles becoming available on a server, instead of
# waiting until a work unit completes (which can take a very long time).
#
# 2) Adding optional load-balance control settings to the server.info file (MAX_SERVER_LAUNCH_DELAY_SECS,
# SERVER_NOMINAL_LOAD_FACTOR, SERVER_MAX_LOAD_FACTOR). These allow dynamic adjustment to grid-level
# (global) parameters that tweak how the load is monitored and balanced across servers.
#
# 3) Added optional DEFAULT_HOST_SUFFIX parameter to server.info file. This defaults to the domain
# suffix of the local host on which prun2 is running. The Schedule::Load modules use fully qualified
# host names, so this makes the internal prun2 host names compatible and thus avoids constant
# translating back and forth between "ds15.ndchealth.com" and "ds15", for example.
# It's also just more correct. :-)
#
# 4) Added a GRID_MIN_PROCESSES setting, which is the minimum total number of processes this specific
# prun2 job will attempt to keep running at any given time. This concept was necessary to help put
# a (small) limit on starvation. This is especially important when the grid is already completely
# consumed with nothing but very long-running processes. When less than GRID_MIN_PROCESSES is
# running for this prun2 job, prun2 will launch a new work unit on the "best" (i.e. least utilized)
# server, even if the load on that server is already at or beyond the SERVER_NOMINAL_LOAD_FACTOR
# (e.g. 100% utilized), but NOT if it's load is at or beyond the SERVER_MAX_LOAD_FACTOR
# (e.g. 130% utilized). Thus, this setting can help minimize starvation (at the risk of overloading
# servers), but it cannot completely avoid it in all circumstances. If prun2 is allowing too
# much starvation for someone's needs, someone can kill other long-running processes and/or
# (less destructively) reduce the load imposed by other prun2 jobs via prun2 control files.
# The default setting for GRID_MIN_PROCESSES is 5% of the maximum possible number of simultaneous
# threads (derived from -r command-line setting). It can be configured via the new GRID_MIN_PROCESSES
# parameter in a control file or via the new -g command line option (below).
#
# The -g command-line option was added to override the default for GRID_MIN_PROCESSES. Setting it
# too high increases the risk of server overload. Even if servers do not get overloaded, your
# co-workers will frown at you for not playing nice. Use of this option is discouraged, as it
# generally goes against the whole purpose load balancing. To minimize the need for *others* to
# use this option, if your work units are known to run for long periods of time (e.g. hours), use
# a host specification (-r option) that uses less than 100% of the servers it runs on. Keep in
# mind that even though starvation may be occuring with your job, it should be temporary.
# When CPU cycles finally become available, a starving prun2 job is more likely to launch a new
# work unit than one that's *not* starving. This behavior was intentionally designed this way in
# order to minimize starvation. However, "temporary" could be a very long time depending on
# how long it takes for a significant number of long-running work units from other prun2
# jobs to complete. You can override this setting via the GRID_MIN_PROCESSES setting in a control
# file.
#
# An alternate way to work around not-so-temporary starvation is to temporarily increase the
# SERVER_MAX_LOAD_FACTOR setting in the server.info file. Setting this too high imposes increased
# risk of server overload. Use with discretion and at your own risk.
#
# 5) Added group write permission to common log file
#

our $DS_BASE_DIR = $ENV{DS_BASE_DIR};
our $DEFAULT_HOST_SUFFIX;

$DEFAULT_SERVER_INFO_FILE = "$DS_BASE_DIR/common/etc/server.info";

our $USER_PROFILE = '$HOME/.bash_profile';
our $DEFAULT_CPU_PRIORITY = 14;
our $MAX_SERVER_FAILURES = 3;

our $DEFAULT_SERVER_NOMINAL_LOAD_FACTOR = 1.0;
our $DEFAULT_SERVER_MAX_LOAD_FACTOR = 1.25;
our $DEFAULT_MIN_SERVER_LAUNCH_DELAY_SECS = 0.5;
our $DEFAULT_MAX_SERVER_LAUNCH_DELAY_SECS = 3;

use Getopt::Std;	# for parsing command line arguments
use Time::Local;
use IO::Handle;
use File::Spec::Functions qw[splitpath canonpath splitdir rel2abs];
use Cwd;
use POSIX ":sys_wait_h";
use Sys::Hostname;
use Schedule::Load::Schedule;
use Data::Dumper;
use Time::HiRes qw( usleep );
use Fcntl qw(:mode);
use List::Util qw(max);

use Schedule::Load::Hosts;
use Schedule::Load;
our $Debug = 0;
$Schedule::Load::Debug = $Debug;
$Schedule::Load::Schedule::Debug = $Debug;
$Schedule::Load::Hosts::Debug = $Debug;

autoflush STDOUT 1;
autoflush STDERR 1;

$PGM = $0;



if (defined($ENV{LOG_DIR})) {
	$LOG_DIR = $ENV{LOG_DIR};

	$YYYYMM = substr(&get_time, 0, 6);

	$LOG_FILE = "$LOG_DIR/${YYYYMM}.prun2.log";
	$COMMON_LOGGING = 0;

	if (! open(COMMON_LOG, ">> $LOG_FILE")) {
		print STDERR "Warning: prun2 will be unable to log to the file $LOG_FILE : $!\n";
	} else {
		$COMMON_LOGGING = 1;

		# add group write permission to log file
		my $perm = (stat $LOG_FILE)[2];
		chmod $perm | S_IWGRP, $LOG_FILE;
	}

	autoflush COMMON_LOG 1;
}

@TERMINATION_SIGNALS = ('HUP', 'INT', 'TERM', 'ABRT', 'BUS', 'FPE', 'ILL', 'QUIT', 'SEGV', 'SYS', 'TRAP');


sub server_name($) {
  my $sname = $_[0];
  my $ret;

	if (defined($DEFAULT_HOST_SUFFIX) && ($sname !~ /[.]/)) {
		$ret = "${sname}${DEFAULT_HOST_SUFFIX}";
	} else {
		$ret = $sname;
	}

	return $ret;
}


sub check_master_list_sanity() {
  my(%temp_master_list);

	# make sure work units are unique

	foreach $work_unit (@master_list) {
		if (exists($temp_master_list{$work_unit})) {
			&print_mesg("ERROR: Work units must be unique, but work unit '$work_unit' occurs more than once\n");
			my_exit(1);
		} else {
			$temp_master_list{$work_unit} = 1;
		}
	}

}


sub sort_master_list() {

	my($num_known_file_sizes) = 0;
	my($fname, $source_file_size, $dev,$ino,$mode,$nlink,$uid,$gid,$rdev,$source_file_size,$atime,$mtime,$ctime,$blksize,$blocks, $num_known_file_sizes, $max_known_file_size, %master_list_sizes);

	if ($SORT_WU_OK) {
		foreach $fname (@master_list) {
			if (-f $fname) {
				($dev,$ino,$mode,$nlink,$uid,$gid,$rdev,$source_file_size,$atime,$mtime,$ctime,$blksize,$blocks) = stat($fname);
				if ($source_file_size =~ /^[1-9][0-9]*$/) {
					$master_list_sizes{$fname} = $source_file_size;
					$num_known_file_sizes++;

					if ($source_file_size > $max_known_file_size) {
						$max_known_file_size = $source_file_size;
					}
				} else {
					$master_list_sizes{$fname} = 'unknown';
				}
			} else {
				$master_list_sizes{$fname} = 'unknown';
			}
		}

		if ($num_known_file_sizes > 0) {
			foreach $fname (keys %master_list_sizes) {
				if ($master_list_sizes{$fname} eq 'unknown') {
					$master_list_sizes{$fname} = $max_known_file_size + 1;
				}
			}

			@master_list = sort { $master_list_sizes{$b} <=> $master_list_sizes {$a} } keys %master_list_sizes;
			$MASTER_LIST_RESORTED = 1;
		}
	}
}


sub print_mesg($;$) {
	my($mesg, $level) = @_;

	if ( (! $QUIET_MODE) or ($mesg =~ /error/i) ) {
			print STDERR $mesg;

			if ($COMMON_LOGGING) {
				if (($level ne 'WU') && ($level ne 'HELP')) {
					$CURR_TIME = &get_time;
					print COMMON_LOG join(' ', ${WU_LOG_TAG}, $USERNAME, $CURR_TIME, $mesg);
				}
			}
	}
}


our $MAX_THREADS;

sub set_max_threads($) {

	$MAX_THREADS = $_[0];

	if (defined($GRID_MIN_PROCESSES) && ($GRID_MIN_PROCESSES > $MAX_THREADS)) {
		&print_mesg("Warning: GRID_MIN_PROCESSES is $GRID_MIN_PROCESSES, which exceeds the current MAX_THREADS ($MAX_THREADS). GRID_MIN_PROCESSES is being reduced to $MAX_THREADS.\n");
		$GRID_MIN_PROCESSES = $MAX_THREADS;
	}
}


sub get_max_threads() {
	return $MAX_THREADS;
}


sub get_time() {
        my (@num_text, @nums, $ni, $mesg_to_print);
        my ($sec,$min,$hour,$mday,$mon,$year,$wday,$yday,$isdst) = localtime(time);
        my @nums = ($mon + 1, $mday, $hour, $min, $sec);

        for ($ni = 0; $ni <= $#nums; $ni++) {
                if ($nums[$ni] < 10 and $nums[$ni] >= 0) {
                        $num_text[$ni] = "0" . $nums[$ni];
                } else {
                        $num_text[$ni] = $nums[$ni];
                }
        }

        ($mon, $mday, $hour, $min, $sec) = @num_text;
        $year += 1900;

        return "${year}${mon}${mday} ${hour}:${min}:${sec}";
}

sub sig_handler_ignore {
       my($sig) = $_[0];
 
       &print_mesg("Warning: $PGM received signal $sig. Ignoring...\n");
}


sub remove_temp_files() {

	if ($TODO_FILE_INDICATOR == 0) {
		if (-f $CONTROL_FILE) {
			$num_deleted = unlink $CONTROL_FILE;
			if ($num_deleted != 1) {
				&print_mesg("Warning: Unable to remove all of the following temp files: $MASTER_TODO_FILE, $CONTROL_FILE\n");
			}
		}

		if ( ($num_fail == 0) or ($remove_temp_wu_on_failures) ) {

			if ((-f $master_done_file) && (! unlink($master_done_file))) {
				&print_mesg("Warning: Unable to remove done file $master_done_file\n");
			}

			if ((-f $MASTER_TODO_FILE) && (! unlink($MASTER_TODO_FILE))) {
				&print_mesg("Warning: Unable to remove master todo file $MASTER_TODO_FILE\n");
			}

		} else {
			print STDERR ("\nNote: Use -f $MASTER_TODO_FILE to retry failed work units.\n");
		}
	}
}


sub close_log() {

	if ($COMMON_LOGGING) {
		$COMMON_LOGGING = 0;
		close(COMMON_LOG);
	}

}

sub my_exit($) {
  my $exit_status = shift;

	&close_log;
	exit($exit_status);
}

sub remote_kill {
  my($sig) = $_[0];

	# Make sure this handler doesn't get called more than once before it can finish the 1st time

	foreach $sig (@TERMINATION_SIGNALS) {
		if ($SIG{$sig} ne 'IGNORE') {
			# assign signal handler for signal unless it is being ignored
			$SIG{$sig} = 'DEFAULT';
		}
	}

	&print_mesg("Note: Work unit $CURRENT_WORKUNIT received signal $sig . Killing remote child process $REMOTE_CHILD_PID on $CURRENT_REMOTE_SERVER .\n", 'WU');

	# Keep running kill command (every 15 seconds) on appropriate pid on appropriate server
	# until kill command returns an error (indicating process has finally died).
	# Start using "kill -9" after 4 failed attempts.

	my $quiet;

	if ($server_info{$CURRENT_REMOTE_SERVER}{'rsh_method'} eq 'ssh') {
		$quiet = '-q -o BatchMode=yes';
	} else {
		$quiet = '';
	}

	my $curr_hostname_adj = $CURRENT_REMOTE_SERVER;

	if (hostname_suffix($CURRENT_REMOTE_SERVER) eq $LOCAL_SUFFIX) {
		$curr_hostname_adj = hostname_prefix($CURRENT_REMOTE_SERVER);
	} else {
		$curr_hostname_adj = $CURRENT_REMOTE_SERVER;
	}

  my $cmd = $server_info{$CURRENT_REMOTE_SERVER}{'rsh_method'} . " $quiet -n $curr_hostname_adj 'kill $REMOTE_CHILD_PID ; sleep 5; tries=1; while kill \$SIG9 $REMOTE_CHILD_PID 2> /dev/null; do sleep 15; tries=\`expr \$tries + 1\` ; if [ \$tries -gt 4 ] ; then SIG9=-9; fi; echo prun2: trying again \\(attempt \$tries\\) to kill \$SIG9 pid $REMOTE_CHILD_PID on $curr_hostname_adj ; done'";

	exec($cmd);

	&print_mesg("Warning: Unable to run kill child process $REMOTE_CHILD_PID on $curr_hostname_adj for work unit $CURRENT_WORKUNIT ! Work unit may still be running!\n");

	my_exit(99);
}

# signal handler routine for abnormal termination of process
sub sig_handler {
  my($sig) = $_[0];
	my($pid, $num_signaled);

  &print_mesg("Warning: $PGM received signal $sig. Killing all currently executing work units..\n", 'WU');
	&remove_temp_files();

	foreach $pid (keys %child) {

			$num_signaled = kill('TERM', $pid);

			if ($num_signaled == 1) {
				&print_mesg("Note: $PGM Sent TERM signal to $child{$pid} work unit (pid = $pid).\n", 'WU');
			} else {
				&print_mesg("Warning: $PGM was unable to send $sig signal to $child{$pid} work unit. Work unit may still be running!\n");
			}
	}

	until (($waited_pid = wait) == -1) {
		&print_mesg("Note: Work unit $child{$waited_pid} appears to have been killed.\n", 'WU');
		delete($child{$waited_pid});
		$KILLED_WU++;
	}

	foreach $pid (keys %child) {
		&print_mesg("Warning: Work unit $child{$pid} (local pid=$pid) was NOT killed!\n");
	}

	&execution_report;

	my_exit(9);
}

# setup signal handler for this (parent) process

foreach $sig (@TERMINATION_SIGNALS) {
        # assign signal handler for signal unless it is being ignored
        if ($SIG{$sig} ne 'IGNORE') {
                $SIG{$sig} = \&sig_handler;
        }
}

# signals to ignore
$SIG{'TTOU'} = \&sig_handler_ignore;

sub execution_report {
  my(@execution_report, $subject_job_name, $subject, $send_to_mail);

	push(@execution_report, "=== prun execution report ===\n");

	if (length($JOB_NAME) > 0) {
		push(@execution_report, "JOB:	$JOB_NAME\n");
		$subject_job_name = $JOB_NAME;
	} else {
		$subject_job_name = $WU_RANGE;
	}

	push(@execution_report, "Work unit source:	$WU_SOURCE\n");
	push(@execution_report, "Work unit range:	$WU_RANGE\n");

	if ($num_fail > 0) {
		push(@execution_report, "Failed work unit executions = $num_fail\n");
		$subject = "$subject_job_name completed with failures";
	} else {
		$subject = "$subject_job_name successfully completed";
	}

	if (($success_retry_exec > 0) or ($failed_retry_exec > 0)) {
		push(@execution_report, "Successful retry executions = $success_retry_exec\n");
		push(@execution_report, "Failed retry executions = $failed_retry_exec\n");
	}

	if ($items_previously_completed > 0) {
		push(@execution_report, "Previously completed work units = $items_previously_completed\n");
	}

	push(@execution_report, "Successful work units = $num_success\n");

	if ($FAILED_DONE_WORK_UNITS > 0) {
		push(@execution_report, "Successful work units not recorded in done file = $FAILED_DONE_WORK_UNITS\n");
	}

	if ($KILLED_WU > 0) {
		push(@execution_report, "Killed work units = $KILLED_WU\n");
	}

	push(@execution_report, "Remaining work units = $NUM_ITEMS_REMAINING\n");

	$elapsed_seconds = time() - $START_TIME;
	push(@execution_report, "Total elapsed time = $elapsed_seconds seconds.\n");

	if ($elapsed_seconds != 0) {

		if (($num_success / ($elapsed_seconds / 3600)) > 0) {
			$time = 'hour';
			$wu_per_time = $num_success / ($elapsed_seconds / 3600);
		} elsif (($num_success / ($elapsed_seconds / 60)) > 0) {
			$time = 'min';
			$wu_per_time = $num_success / ($elapsed_seconds / 60);
		} elsif (($num_success / $elapsed_seconds) > 0) {
			$time = 'sec';
			$wu_per_time = $num_success / $elapsed_seconds;
		}

		if (defined($wu_per_time)) {
			push(@execution_report, sprintf("Throughput = %.1f work units / %s\n", $wu_per_time, $time));
		}
	}

	if (($MAIL_ON_SUCCESS) and (! $num_fail > 0)) {
		foreach $email_address (@success_email_addresses) {
			$email_address_list{$email_address} = 1;
		}
	}

	if (($MAIL_ON_FAILURE) and ($num_fail > 0)) {
		foreach $email_address (@failure_email_addresses) {
			$email_address_list{$email_address} = 1;
		}
	}

	if ((($MAIL_ON_SUCCESS) and (! $num_fail > 0)) or (($MAIL_ON_FAILURE) and ($num_fail > 0))) {
		$email_addresses = join(',', keys %email_address_list);

		if (open(MAIL, "| mail -s '$subject' $email_addresses")) {
			$send_to_mail = 1;
		} else {
			push(@execution_report, "Warning: Could not start mail process to send to $address_list\n");
		}
	}

	foreach $report_line (@execution_report) {
		&print_mesg($report_line);

		if ($send_to_mail) {
			print(MAIL $report_line);
		}
	}

	if ($send_to_mail) {
		close(MAIL);
	}
}

sub file_updated() {
  my($fname) = shift;

	if (-r $fname) {
		($dev,$ino,$mode,$nlink,$uid,$gid,$rdev,$source_file_size,$atime,$mtime,$ctime,$blksize,$blocks) = stat($fname);

		if (! exists($LAST_FILE_MTIME{$fname})) {
			$LAST_FILE_MTIME{$fname} = $mtime;
			return 1;
		}

		if ($mtime == $LAST_FILE_MTIME{$fname}) {
			return 0;
		}

		$LAST_FILE_MTIME{$fname} = $mtime;
		return 1;

	} else {
		if (exists($LAST_FILE_MTIME{$fname})) {		# file previously existed
			delete $LAST_FILE_MTIME{$fname};
			return 1;	# force update, since file was removed
		} else {
			return undef;
		}
	}
}

sub read_control_info() {
	my($val, $server_name, $max_threads, $found_group, $parm, $read_priority);

		%CONTROL_INFO = ();

		if (-r $CONTROL_FILE) {
			open(CTL, "< $CONTROL_FILE") || return $max_threads;

			while (<CTL>) {

				$val = $_;
				chomp($val);

				next if ($val =~ /^\s*$/);	# skip blank lines
				next if ($val =~ /^\s*#/);	# skip commented lines

				$val =~ s/^\s+//;
				$val =~ s/\s+$//;

				# check for "parm = value"

				if ($val =~ /^\s*([a-z0-9_]+)\s*=\s*['"]?([a-z0-9_.]+)['"]?\s*$/i) {
					($parm, $val) = (uc($1), $2);

					if ($parm eq 'PRIORITY') {

						if ($val =~ /^normal$/i) {
							$val = 0;
						} elsif ($val !~ /^\s*(\d+)\s*$/) {
							&print_mesg("Warning: PRIORITY value of '$val' in control file $CONTROL_FILE is not a positive integer. Ignoring.\n");
							next;
						}

						if ($val > 19) {
							&print_mesg("Warning: Max PRIORITY value is 19 (lowest priority), so read priority of '$val' will have the same effect as specifying 19\n");
						}

						$read_priority = $val;

					} elsif ($parm eq 'GRID_MIN_PROCESSES') {
						if (($val =~ /^\d+$/) && ($val >= 0)) {
							if ($val != $GRID_MIN_PROCESSES) {
								&print_mesg("Note: Changing GRID_MIN_PROCESSES from $GRID_MIN_PROCESSES to $val via control file.\n");
								$GRID_MIN_PROCESSES = $val;
							}
						} else {
							&print_mesg("Warning: GRID_MIN_PROCESSES value of '$val' in control file $CONTROL_FILE is not >= 0. Ignoring.\n");
							next;
						}
					}
				} else {

					# check for "servername:processes" or "groupname:processes"

					if (! ($_ =~ /[:,]/)) {
						&print_mesg("Warning: cannot understand control file instruction '$_' . Ignoring. Accepted syntax is 'x:#', where x is servername or group name, and # is number of work units to keep running on each server.\n");
						next;
					}

					($server_name, $max_threads) = split('[:,]', $val);

					if ($server_name eq '') {
						next;
					}

					if (! ($max_threads =~ /^[0-9]+/)) {
						&print_mesg("Warning: max threads value of $max_threads for server $server_name in control file $CONTROL_FILE is not valid. Ignoring.\n");
						next;
					}

					$CONTROL_INFO{$server_name} = $max_threads;
				}
			}

			close(CTL);

			if (defined($read_priority)) {

				if (defined($workunit_priority)) {

					if ($read_priority != $workunit_priority) {

						if ($argv[0] eq 'nice') {

							if ($argv[1] ne '-n') {
								&print_mesg("ERROR: cannot find '-n' parameter to 'nice' command. prun2 bug exists!\n");
								my_exit(1);
							}

							if ($argv[2] !~ /^\d+$/) {
								&print_mesg("ERROR: cannot find numeric argument to 'nice -n' parameter. prun2 bug exists!\n");
								my_exit(1);
							}

							if ($workunit_priority != $argv[2]) {
								&print_mesg("ERROR: current priority of '$workunit_priority' does not match expected priority of '" . $argv[2] . "' . prun2 bug exists!\n");
								my_exit(1);
							}

							&print_mesg("Note: CPU scheduling priority for remaining work units has changed from $workunit_priority to $read_priority\n");
							$argv[2] = $read_priority;
							$workunit_priority = $read_priority;
					}
				}
			} else {

				if ($argv[0] eq 'nice') {
					&print_mesg("ERROR: Attempting to establish priority of '$read_priority'. Found existing 'nice' command prefix, but did not expect it to be there\n");
					my_exit(1);
				}

				&print_mesg("Note: CPU scheduling priority for remaining work units will be $read_priority\n");

				@argv = ('nice', '-n', $read_priority, @argv);
				$workunit_priority = $read_priority;
			}
		}
	}
}

sub curr_load($) {
  my $ho = $_[0];

#	my $adj_load = $ho->adj_load;
#	my $load = $ho->total_load;
#	my $cpus = $ho->cpus;
#	my $total_pctcpu = $ho->total_pctcpu;

#	my $pct_based_load = int($total_pctcpu / 100 + 0.6) / $cpus;
#	my $adj_based_load = $adj_load / $cpus;
#	my $load_factor = $load / $cpus;

	return $ho->total_load / $ho->cpus;
}

our $SCHEDULER;

our $SERVER_MAX_LOAD_FACTOR;
our $SERVER_NOMINAL_LOAD_FACTOR;
our $MIN_SERVER_LAUNCH_DELAY_SECS = $DEFAULT_MIN_SERVER_LAUNCH_DELAY_SECS;
our $MAX_SERVER_LAUNCH_DELAY_SECS;

our $GRID_MIN_PROCESSES;

our $MAX_RND_THRESH_ADJ = 0.3;

sub grid_min_processes() {

	if (defined($GRID_MIN_PROCESSES)) {
		return $GRID_MIN_PROCESSES;
	} else {
		my $gmp = int(0.05 * get_max_threads + 0.5);
		$gmp = 1 if ($gmp < 1);

		return $gmp;
	}
}

sub can_launch($$) {
  my ($threads_running, $curr_load_factor) = @_;

	if (
			($curr_load_factor < $SERVER_NOMINAL_LOAD_FACTOR) ||
			(($threads_running < grid_min_processes()) && ($curr_load_factor < $SERVER_MAX_LOAD_FACTOR))
		) {
		return 1;
	} else {
		return 0;
	}
}


our $MAX_VIRTUAL_MEMORY_LOAD_FACTOR = 1.5;
our $MAX_RSS_MEMORY_LOAD_FACTOR = 0.9;

sub high_memory($$$) {
  my ($virtual_mem, $rss_mem, $physical_mem) = @_;

	if ((! defined($virtual_mem)) || (! defined($physical_mem)) || (! defined($rss_mem))) {
#print "debug undef: virtual_mem = $virtual_mem, physical mem = $physical_mem, rss_mem = $rss_mem\n";
		return undef;
	}

	if (($virtual_mem > 0) && ($physical_mem > 0) && ($rss_mem > 0)) {
#print "debug: virtual_mem = $virtual_mem, physical mem = $physical_mem, rss mem = $rss_mem\n";
		if (
				($virtual_mem / $physical_mem > $MAX_VIRTUAL_MEMORY_LOAD_FACTOR) ||
				($rss_mem / $physical_mem > $MAX_RSS_MEMORY_LOAD_FACTOR)
			) {
			return 1
		} else {
			return 0;
		}
	}

	return undef;
}


our $MIN_SECONDS_TIL_RSS_FULL = 200;
our $MIN_SECONDS_TIL_VIRT_FULL = 300;

sub accelerating_mem($$$$$$) {
  my ($curr_mem, $prev_mem, $phys_mem, $curr_time, $prev_time, $min_seconds) = @_;

	return 0; # this function disabled here.

	if ((! defined($curr_mem)) || (! defined($prev_mem)) || (! defined($phys_mem)) || (! defined($curr_time)) || (! defined($prev_time)) || (! defined($min_seconds))) {
#print "curr_mem = $curr_mem, prev_mem = $prev_mem, phys_mem = $phys_mem, curr_time = $curr_time, prev_time = $prev_time\n";
		return undef;
	}

	if (($curr_mem > 0) && ($prev_mem > 0) && ($phys_mem > 0) && ($curr_time > 0) && ($prev_time > 0)) {
		my $num_seconds_elapsed = $curr_time - $prev_time;
		#my $rss_diff_per_sec = ($curr_mem - $prev_mem) / $phys_mem / $num_seconds;

		my $free_bytes = $phys_mem - $curr_mem;

#		if ($free_bytes <= 0) {
#			return undef;
#		}

		if ($num_seconds_elapsed < 0) {
			return undef;
		}

		if ($num_seconds_elapsed == 0) {
			$num_seconds_elapsed = 0.5;	# we're faking it for an approximation, since granularity is 1 second
		}

		my $bytes_per_sec = ($curr_mem - $prev_mem) / $num_seconds_elapsed;

		if ($bytes_per_sec == 0) {
			return 0;
		}

		my $secs_til_full = int($free_bytes / $bytes_per_sec);


		if (abs($secs_til_full) < $min_seconds) {
			$Debug && print "debug: seconds until full = $secs_til_full (min = $min_seconds). elapsed = $num_seconds_elapsed .\n";
			return 1;
		} else {
			return 0;
		}
	}

	return undef;
}

sub get_avail_server_alt($$) {
  my $avail_servers = shift;
	my $threads_running = shift;

	# try picking server with the lowest load
	my ($curr_min_load_factor, $curr_host);

	foreach my $server (keys %{$avail_servers}) {
		next if (! can_launch($threads_running, $avail_servers->{$server}->{curr_load_factor}));

		if (($avail_servers->{$server}->{curr_load_factor} < $curr_min_load_factor) || (! defined($curr_min_load_factor))) {
			$curr_min_load_factor = $avail_servers->{$server}->{curr_load_factor};
